SQL Server Grouping Workbench

= A gentle lesson about GROUP BY on the Nursery Slopes develops = gradually into a wild ride off-piste amongst the pine-trees.

=09

This Workbench is about using the GROUP BY clause in a = SQL Statement. It is designed so it can be pasted straight into SSMS or the= Query Analyser, though to run the examples, you=E2=80=99ll need the data f= ile too. Just click the =E2=80=9CCODE DOWNLOAD=E2=80=9D link at the bottom = of this article. Also included in the download bundle is the original SQL f= ile, if you need it.

Contents

  • Introduction
  • Removing Duplicates
  • Simple Reporting
  • Grouping and Pivot Tables
  • Enumerating the Group members
  • Ranging
  • Grouping as a utility
  • Questions

Introduction

Like all these workbench articles, the whole point is to try different t= hings out, improve on the code, and learn in a practical way. If you=E2=80= =99re like us, and find you can take in information only after real practic= e doing things for real then this article is for you.

If you think that it is too elementary, move to the end of the article a= nd test out your knowledge by answering all the questions (Yes, the editor = is giving away prizes for the best answers he receives. Insist on the glori= ous USB Red-Gate pendant).

Aggregations in SQL are very simple to do, but can cause a lot of confus= ion due to the word =E2=80=98Group=E2=80=99. The result you get from a grou= ping does not consist of the individual records but a collection or =E2=80= =98aggregation=E2=80=99 of records.

A pack of playing cards is a group of 52 playing cards. If you were to g= roup a pack of cards by colour, you=E2=80=99d have two =E2=80=98rows=E2=80= =99 of 26 cards; if you grouped by suit, there would be four =E2=80=98rows= =E2=80=99 with 13 in each. You could group them by their rank/court attribu= te, or in other ways. The point is that the result is always an aggregate, = even if there is only one member in the collection.

Each row in the result of a GROUP BY represents a collectio= n, or grouping. You can get the values for the number of records in each co= llection, or grouping, or the sum, average, and so on of numeric values, or= the max or min of strings, but to ask for individual values makes no sense= if you haven=E2=80=99t grouped by that value.

Sometimes, you will use an aggregate function in a SELECT S= tatement without using a GROUP BY clause. There is an implicit= grouping of the entire result into one row, which is why you can only use = aggregate functions in such a case, and will get one row returned.

GROUP BY statements are the bedrock of reporting in SQL.

The built-in aggregate functions are=E2=80=A6

Common ones

=09
1
2
3
4
5

sum([all|distinct] expr.)  = ; Total of the (distinct) values in the expression

max(= expr.)   &nb= sp;            =   Highest value in the expression
min(expr.)     &n= bsp;            = ;Lowest value <= span class=3D"crayon-k ">in the expression

=09

Var(expr.)&nbs= p;            &= nbsp;   The Variance of= the expression values
Varp(expr.)     &n= bsp;            = ;  The population Variance of the expression values

Checksum functions

=09
1

Checksum(expr.)          =       Returns= the= checksum value

Checksum_agg=
([all|distinct] expr.)     Returns<= span class=3D"crayon-h"> the checksum of the= NON-NULL values in a group.&nb= sp; 

(You can use sum and avg with numeric columns only =E2=80=93 int, = smallint, TinyIntBigint decimal, numeric, float, SmallMoney and money. You cannot use min and max with= bit datatypes. You cannot use aggregate functions other than count(*= ) with text and image datatypes.)

We=E2=80=99ll start with some simple manoevres and then finish off with = a few wheelies and handbrake-turns.

As sample data, we=E2=80=99ll take a list of all oil-producing countries= in the world and their oil-production.

Create a new database or use your =E2=80=98practice=E2=80=99 development= Database and then create this.

Removing Duplicates

Before we get stuck into doing reporting, I=E2=80=99ll illustrate how si= mple it is to remove duplicates from tables using grouping.

Of course, if you are going to remove duplicates, you will really want t= o move them to another table for forensic analysis to find out how it happe= ned and whether they are valid entries. Here is our Duplicates table:

=09
1
2
3
4
5
6
7
8
CREATE TABLE [dbo].[Duplica= tes](
   [OilProducer_I= D] = [int] IDENTITY(1,1) NOT NULL,
   [Duplicate_ID] [int],
   [country= ] [= varchar](30) NOT NULL, =
   = [BarrelsPerDay ] [int] NOT NULL,
   [Continent] [varchar](80) NOT NULL,
   [Region] [varchar]= (80) NOT NULL
)<= /span> ON [PRIMARY]

Let=E2=80=99s maliciously create some duplicates!

=09
1
2
3
4
5
6
INSERT INTO OilProducers(Country,BarrelsPerDay,continent, region)
   SELECT Country,BarrelsPerDay,continent, region  
     &nb= sp;   FROM OilProducers WHERE country LIKE <= /span>'A%' =
INSERT INTO OilProducers(Country,BarrelsPerDay ,continent, region)
   SELECT Country,BarrelsPerDay,continent, region  
     &nb= sp;  FROM OilProducers WHERE country BETWEEN= 'A' AND 'E'
=

You can then easily see these duplicates by:

=09
1
2
3
4
SELECT 'First_ID'=3DMAX(OilProducer_ID), 'No.InTable'=3DCOUNT(*)
 = ;  FROM OilProducers
   GROUP BY= country  
 = ;  HAVING COUNT(= *)<= span class=3D"crayon-o">>1
=

Notice that we use a HAVING clause. This is because we are = selecting only those rows that contain more than one row in the original ta= ble (we could have checked only part of the original table by using the WHERE clause. A WHERE clause cannot contain an aggre= gate function of course, but the HAVING clause can.

So we move them to another table to check them to make sure. We wrap thi= s up in a transaction just in case anything goes wrong, as we don=E2=80=99t= want to lose a record that might turn out to be legit.

=09
1
2
3
4

-- start of routine=
DECLARE @found INT
DECLARE @Errorhappened INT
DECLAR= E @= OtherErrorhappened= INT
BEGIN TRANSACTION
=
WHILE COALESCE(@found,1= )>0  
 =       AND<= span class=3D"crayon-h"> COALESCE(@ErrorHappened,0) =3D0
&nbs= p;      AND COALESCE<= span class=3D"crayon-sy">(@OtherErrorHappened,0)=3D0
   BEGIN
   INSERT INTO Duplicates (Duplicate_ID,country,BarrelsPerDay,continent,region)
       SELECT Oil= Producer_ID,country,= BarrelsPerDay,continent,region
&n= bsp;      FROM OilProducers WHERE= oilProducer_ID IN (
     =       SELECT MAX(OilProducer_ID<= span class=3D"crayon-sy">)
          &= nbsp;     FROM OilProducers
  =              GROUP = BY country  =
        &nbs= p;      HAVING COUNT(*)>1)
   SELECT @Errorhappened=3D@@= Error, @found=3D@@Rowcount
   DELETE FROM OilProducers WHERE oilProducer_ID IN (
        &= nbsp;  SELECT MAX(OilProducer_ID)
 = ;            &n= bsp; FROM <= /span>OilProducers=
       &n= bsp;       GR= OUP BY country<= span class=3D"crayon-h">  
 &nb= sp;            = HAVING COUNT(= *)>1)--the HAVING clause has to be used as
&nb= sp;            =             &nb= sp;        --we have to select rows after the
&n= bsp;            = ;            &n= bsp;        --aggregation
   SELECT @OtherErrorHappened=3D@@Error
   END
IF @errorHappened<>0 or <= /span>@OtherError= Happened &l= t;>0 ROLLBACK TRANSACTION
ELSE COMMIT TRANSACTION  &nb= sp; 
--end of routine
<= /td>

Simple Reporting

What about getting a summary of oil production per continent?

=09
1
2
3
4
SELECT [Barrels per day ]=3DSUM(BarrelsPerDay), continent
   FROM OilProducers  
<= span class=3D"crayon-h">   GROUP<= /span> BY continent --each row should be= a continent
   ORDER BY SUM(Barre= lsPerDay) = DESC --in descending order

We are grouping by continent and get back seven records, each of which r= epresents a collection of oil producers in the same continent.

Grand totals are easy:

   = [continent= ]=3DCOALESCE(= continent,= 'Total (world production)'),

   FROM OilProducers  
&nbs= p;  GROUP BY continent WITH rollup--each row shoul= d be a continent
    ORDER BY grouping(continent) ASC,SUM(BarrelsPerDay) DES= C

We used the grouping() function to order the total at the e= nd we used WITH ROLLUP to compute the total. It can be very us= eful for running sums and running averages.

=

ON g.n=3Df= .n<= span class=3D"crayon-h">

Grouping and Pivot Tables

So let=E2=80=99s get a bit harder and do a pivot table relating regions = and continents with column and row totals.

=09
1
2
3
4
5

SELECT [region/continent ]=3D= CONVERT(CH= AR(25),COALESCE(region,'Total')),
   'Asia'=3DSUM(= CASE WHEN continent =3D 'Asia' THEN BarrelsPerDay ELSE 0 END),
   'North A.'<= /span>=3DSUM(CASE WHEN continent =3D'North America'  
         &= nbsp;           &nbs= p;            &= nbsp;         THEN BarrelsPerDay ELSE 0 = END) ,
=
   'Latin A.'=3DSUM(CASE WHEN continent =3D'Latin America and the Caribbean'&nb= sp; 
      &= nbsp;           &nbs= p;            &= nbsp;           &nbs= p;THEN BarrelsPerDay <= /span>ELSE = 0 END),
=    'Africa'=3DSUM(CASE= WHEN continent =3D'Africa' THEN BarrelsPerDay ELSE 0 END),
=    'Russ= ia'=3DSUM(CASE= WHEN continent =3D'Russia' THEN BarrelsPerDay  ELSE 0 END),<= /span>
   = 'Europe'=3D= SUM(CASE WHEN continent =3D'Europe' THEN BarrelsPerDay ELSE 0 END)<= span class=3D"crayon-sy">,
   'Oceania'= =3DSUM(CASE WHEN continent =3D'Oceania' = THEN Barrel= sPerDay ELS= E 0= END),
   'sum'=3DSUM(BarrelsPerDay)
FROM OilProducers
GROUP BY region
   WITH rollup
   ORDER  <= span class=3D"crayon-k">BY grouping(region),SUM(BarrelsPerDay) DESC

The =E2=80=98order by grouping=E2=80=99 trick ensures that the total com= es in the right place on the last row!

Enumerating the Group members

This is all OK but a lot of people want, and expect, to have a list of a= ll the constituents of their grouping in the result. They don=E2=80=99t lik= e DBAs laughing and saying it isn=E2=80=99t possible. There are now CLR Agg= regation routines that do it, but here is a method that works on SQL 2000. = Not a cursor in sight! (it works a lot better in 2005 with VaRCHAR(MA= X)).

Ranging

SELECT
[range]=3D'No. of Countries',  
[< <= span class=3D"crayon-cn">10,000 bpd]=3DSUM(CASE <= /span>WHEN = Barrelsperday<<= /span>10000 THEN 1 ELSE 0 = END),
[10,000 to 10= 0,000]=3DSUM(CASE WHEN Barrelsperday BETWEEN 10000 AND 1000= 00  
            &n= bsp;           THEN 1 ELSE 0  
           &= nbsp;        END),
[100,000 to 1m bpd]=3DSUM(<= span class=3D"crayon-k">CASE WHEN Barrelsperday BETWEEN 100001 AND 1000000  
          &= nbsp;           &nbs= p; THEN 1 ELSE 0  
         =            END),
[1m to 10m bpd]=3DSUM(CASE WHEN <= /span>Barrelsperday BETWEEN = 1000001 AND <= span class=3D"crayon-cn">10000000 &nbs= p;
       &= nbsp;           &nbs= p;     THEN 1 ELSE 0=   
     &nb= sp;            =   END),
[more than 10m bpd]=3DSU= M(CASE WHEN Barrelsperday= > 10000000  THEN 1 ELSE 0 END)
FROM OilProducers
 
--or by row...
SELECT [category]=3DCASE WHEN Barrelsperday<10000 THEN = '1/ > 10,000 bpd'  
   WHEN= Barrelsperday BETWEEN 10000   AND 100000= THEN '2/ 10,000 to 100,000 '=
  =   WHEN Barrelsperday BETWEEN 100001  AND 1000000 THEN= '3/ 100,000 to 1m bpd'
    WHEN Barrelsperday BETWEEN 1000001 AND 10000000 THEN '4/ 1m to 10m bpd'
    WHEN<= /span> Barrelsperd= ay > 10000000  THEN= '5/ more t= han 10m bpd' END,
   [<= /span>total]=3DSUM(BarrelsperDay),
   [No. of Co= untries]= =3DCOUNT(<= /span>*)
FROM OilProducers
GROUP BY CASE WHEN Barrelsperday<10000 &n= bsp;THEN '1/ > 10,000 bpd'  
   WHEN Barrelsperday BETWEEN 10000   AND 100000 THEN '2/ 10,000 to 100,000'
    W= HEN Barrels= perday BET= WEEN 10000= 1  AND 100= 0000 THEN '3/ 100,000 = to 1m bpd'
&n= bsp;   WHEN Barrelsperday BETWEEN 1000001 AND 10000000 THEN '4/ 1m to 10m bpd'
    WHEN Barrelsperday > 10000000  <= span class=3D"crayon-k">THEN '5/ more than 10m bpd' END

CREATE FUNCTION OilOutputCategory =
(
   @OilOutput INT
)
RETUR= NS VARCHAR<= /span>(30= )
AS
BEGIN
RETUR= N CASE WHEN @OilOutput<10000 THEN '1/ > 10,000 bpd'  
   WHEN= @<= span class=3D"crayon-i">OilOutput BETWEEN 10000   AND 100000 THEN '2/ 10,000 to 100,000'
<= span class=3D"crayon-h">    WHEN = @OilOutput = BETWEEN 100001 =  AND = 1000000 THEN <= span class=3D"crayon-s">'3/ 100,000 to 1m bpd'
    WHEN @OilOutput BETWEEN 1000001 AND = 10000000 <= /span>THEN &n= bsp;'4/ 1m to 10m bpd'
    WHEN @OilOutput > 10000000  THEN '5/ more than 10m bpd' END
 
END
GO
--so the query becomes...
=

   [total]=3DSUM= (BarrelsperDay),
   [<= /span>producers]<= /span>=3DCOUNT(*)
FROM OilProducers
GROUP B= Y dbo.OilOutputCatego= ry(Barrels= PerDay)

Grouping as a utility

One can use grouping in a variety of ways that have nothing to do with r= eporting . Here is an example of using GROUP BY to help produc= e a table by splitting a delimited list. It needs the Number Helper Table (= You=E2=80=99ll have to refer to the =E2=80=98Helper Table Workbench to find= out about that).

CREATE FUNCTION [dbo].[uftS= plitStringGroup]
(
= @DelimitedList VARCHAR (8000),
@Delimiter VARCHAR(20)=3D','
)
RETURNS <= /span>
@Results TABLE
(
Se= qNo INT IDENTITY(1, 1),
Item VARCHAR(8000)
)
AS
BEGIN
DECLARE @String VARCHAR(8000)
DEC= LARE @LenDelimiter INT
&nbs= p;
= SELECT @String=3D@Delimiter+@DelimitedList+@Delimiter,
   @LenDelimiter=3DLEN( @Delimiter)
 
INSER= T INTO @results (item)
   SELECT SUBSTRING(@string,
&n= bsp;            = ;        s1.number= +@<= span class=3D"crayon-i">LenDelimiter,
   = ;            &n= bsp;     MIN(s2.number)-s1.numb= er-@LenDelimiter)
  &nb= sp;  FROM    (SELECT [string]=3D @Str= ing )f
<= div class=3D"crayon-line" id=3D"crayon-6039884342e4c759002991-25">   CROSS<= span class=3D"crayon-h"> JOIN numbers s1  
   INNER JOIN numbers s2 O= N s1= .number< s2.number
   WHERE s1.number&= lt;=3DLEN = (@string)
       AND  s2.number<=3DLEN (@string)
&n= bsp;      AND SUBSTRING(@string,s1.number,@LenDelimiter)=3D@Delimiter
       AND SUBSTRING(@string,s2.number,@LenDelimiter)=3D@Delimiter
&n= bsp;  GROUP BY s1.number
=
RETURN
END
/*
select * from uftSplitStringGroup('first,second,third',default)
<= div class=3D"crayon-line" id=3D"crayon-6039884342e4c759002991-36">select * from u= ftSplitStringGroup('<>this is something<>something else<>','<>'<= span class=3D"crayon-sy">)
select * from uftSp= litStringGroup(
'Turke= y,Bahrain,Yemen,Syria,United Arab Emirates,Saudi Arabia,Qatar,Kuwait',',')
